      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Kuwait" title="Art of Kuwait">Art of Kuwait</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kuwait has the oldest <a href="/wiki/Modern_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern arts">modern arts</a> movement in the Arabian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-movemnt_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movemnt-319">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Beginning in 1936, Kuwait was the first Gulf Arab country to grant scholarships in the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-movemnt_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movemnt-319">[319]</a></sup> The Kuwaiti artist <a href="/wiki/Mojeb_al-Dousari" title="Mojeb al-Dousari">Mojeb al-Dousari</a> was the earliest recognized <a href="/wiki/Visual_artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual artist">visual artist</a> in the Gulf Arab region.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> He is regarded as the founder of <a href="/wiki/Portrait" title="Portrait">portrait</a> art in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> The Sultan Gallery was the first professional Arab art gallery in the Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kuwait is home to more than <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Kuwait#Art_galleries" title="Art of Kuwait">30 art galleries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> In recent years, Kuwait's contemporary art scene has boomed.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalifa Al-Qattan">Khalifa Al-Qattan</a> was the first artist to hold a <a href="/wiki/Solo_exhibition" title="Solo exhibition">solo exhibition</a> in Kuwait. He founded a new art theory in the early 1960s known as "circulism".<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> Other notable Kuwaiti artists include <a href="/wiki/Sami_Mohammad" title="Sami Mohammad">Sami Mohammad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thuraya_Al-Baqsami" title="Thuraya Al-Baqsami">Thuraya Al-Baqsami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suzan_Bushnaq" title="Suzan Bushnaq">Suzan Bushnaq</a>. </p>
      <p>The government organizes various <a href="/wiki/Arts_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts festivals">arts festivals</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Al_Qurain_Cultural_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qurain Cultural Festival">Al Qurain Cultural Festival</a> and Formative Arts Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> The Kuwait International Biennial was inaugurated in 1967,<sup id="cite_ref-biennial_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biennial-336">[336]</a></sup> more than 20 Arab and foreign countries have participated in the biennial.<sup id="cite_ref-biennial_336-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biennial-336">[336]</a></sup> Prominent participants include <a href="/wiki/Layla_Al-Attar" title="Layla Al-Attar">Layla Al-Attar</a>. In 2004, the Al Kharafi Biennial for Contemporary Arab Art was inaugurated. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kuwait" title="Music of Kuwait">Music of Kuwait</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kuwait is the birthplace of various popular musical genres, such as <a href="/wiki/Sawt_(music)" title="Sawt (music)">sawt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kwq_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwq-337">[337]</a></sup> Kuwaiti music has considerably influenced the music culture in other <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> (GCC) countries.<sup id="cite_ref-rvo_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rvo-338">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kwq_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwq-337">[337]</a></sup> Traditional Kuwaiti music is a reflection of the country's seafaring heritage,<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> which is known for genres such as <a href="/wiki/Fijiri" title="Fijiri">fijiri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ya_Bahr_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ya_Bahr-340">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qdl_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qdl-342">[342]</a></sup> Kuwait pioneered <a href="/wiki/Khaliji_(music)" title="Khaliji (music)">contemporary Khaliji music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shart_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shart-343">[343]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pers_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pers-344">[344]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shartw_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shartw-345">[345]</a></sup> Kuwaitis were the first commercial recording artists in the Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-shart_343-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shart-343">[343]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pers_344-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pers-344">[344]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shartw_345-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shartw-345">[345]</a></sup> The first known Kuwaiti recordings were made between 1912 and 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" title="Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre</a> contains the largest opera house in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> Kuwait is home to various <a href="/wiki/Music_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Music festivals">music festivals</a>, including the International Music Festival hosted by the National Council for Culture, Arts and Letters (NCCAL).<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup> Kuwait has several academic institutions specializing in university-level <a href="/wiki/Music_education" title="Music education">music education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-351">[351]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-352">[352]</a></sup> The Higher Institute of Musical Arts was established by the government to provide <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor's degrees">bachelor's degrees</a> in music.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_350-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_351-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-351">[351]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_352-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-352">[352]</a></sup> In addition, the College of Basic Education offers bachelor's degrees in music education.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_350-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_351-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-351">[351]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_352-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-352">[352]</a></sup> The Institute of Musical Studies offers degrees equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_350-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_352-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-352">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_351-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-351">[351]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_literature" title="Kuwaiti literature">Kuwaiti literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kuwait has, in recent years, produced several prominent contemporary writers such as <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Fahd_Ismail" title="Ismail Fahd Ismail">Ismail Fahd Ismail</a>, author of over twenty novels and numerous short story collections.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup> There is also evidence that Kuwaiti literature has long been interactive with <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_literature" title="French literature">French literature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Kuwait" title="List of museums in Kuwait">List of museums in Kuwait</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beitalsadu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/220px-Beitalsadu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/330px-Beitalsadu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/440px-Beitalsadu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="634"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beitalsadu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sadu_House" title="Sadu House">Sadu House</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The new <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District" title="Kuwait National Cultural District">Kuwait National Cultural District</a> (KNCD) consists of various cultural venues including <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre">Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park" title="Al Shaheed Park">Al Shaheed Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_(Kuwait)" title="Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)">Al Salam Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_147-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kncd2_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd2-148">[148]</a></sup> With a capital cost of more than US$1&nbsp;billion, it is one of the largest cultural districts in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_147-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-147">[147]</a></sup> The Abdullah Salem Cultural Centre is the largest museum complex in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup> The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network" title="Global Cultural Districts Network">Global Cultural Districts Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcdn_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcdn-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several Kuwaiti museums are devoted to <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Tareq_Rajab_Museum" title="Tareq Rajab Museum">Tareq Rajab Museums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dar_al_Athar_al_Islamiyyah" title="Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah">Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah</a> cultural centres.<sup id="cite_ref-modmus_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-357">[357]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[358]</a></sup> The Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah cultural centres include education wings, conservation labs, and research libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dai_361-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai-361">[361]</a></sup> There are several <a href="/wiki/Libraries" class="mw-redirect" title="Libraries">art libraries</a> in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dai_361-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai-361">[361]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalifa Al-Qattan">Khalifa Al-Qattan</a>'s Mirror House is the most popular art museum in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> Many museums in Kuwait are private enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-trans_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-365">[365]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modmus_357-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-357">[357]</a></sup> In contrast to the top-down approach in other Gulf states, museum development in Kuwait reflects a greater sense of civic identity and demonstrates the strength of civil society in Kuwait, which has produced many independent cultural enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modmus_357-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-357">[357]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trans_365-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-365">[365]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sadu_House" title="Sadu House">Sadu House</a> is among Kuwait's most important cultural institutions. <a href="/wiki/Bait_Al-Othman_Museum" title="Bait Al-Othman Museum">Bait Al-Othman</a> is the largest museum specializing in Kuwait's history. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Scientific_Center" title="Kuwait Scientific Center">The Scientific Center</a> is one of the largest science museums in the Middle East. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art_(Kuwait)" title="Museum of Modern Art (Kuwait)">Museum of Modern Art</a> showcases the history of modern art in Kuwait and the region.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Museum" title="Kuwait National Museum">National Museum</a>, established in 1983, has been described as "underused and overlooked".<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/150px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/225px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/300px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="835"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 372&nbsp;m (1,220&nbsp;ft) tall <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Telecommunications_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Telecommunications Tower">Kuwait Telecommunications Tower</a> (leftmost) is the main communication tower of Kuwait.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kuwait's media is annually classified as "partly free" in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Press" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of Press">Freedom of Press</a> survey by Freedom House.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> Since 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-prfr_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfr-370">[370]</a></sup> Kuwait has frequently earned the highest ranking of all Arab countries in the annual <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> by Reporters Without Borders.<sup id="cite_ref-fanak_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fanak-371">[371]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isr_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isr-372">[372]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indi_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indi-373">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indextwo_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indextwo-374">[374]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ofa_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofa-378">[378]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup> In 2009, 2011, 2013 and 2014, Kuwait surpassed <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> as the country with the greatest press freedom in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-fanak_371-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fanak-371">[371]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isr_372-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isr-372">[372]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indi_373-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indi-373">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indextwo_374-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indextwo-374">[374]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ofa_378-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofa-378">[378]</a></sup> Kuwait is also frequently ranked as the Arab country with the greatest press freedom in Freedom House's annual Freedom of Press survey.<sup id="cite_ref-lead_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lead-380">[380]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[386]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kuwait produces more <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Kuwait" title="List of newspapers in Kuwait">newspapers and magazines</a> per capita than its neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup> There are limits to Kuwait's press freedom; while criticism of the government and ruling family members is permitted, Kuwait's constitution criminalizes criticism of the Emir. </p>
      <p>The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_News_Agency" title="Kuwait News Agency">Kuwait News Agency</a> (KUNA) is the largest media house in the country. The Ministry of Information regulates the media industry in Kuwait. </p>
      <p>Kuwait has 15 satellite television channels, of which four are controlled by the Ministry of Information. State-owned <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Television" title="Kuwait Television">Kuwait Television</a> (KTV) offered first colored broadcast in 1974 and operates five television channels. Government-funded Radio Kuwait also offers daily informative programming in several languages including <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farsi" class="mw-redirect" title="Farsi">Farsi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, and English on the <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Shortwave">SW</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG/220px-Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG/330px-Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG/440px-Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1225"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium-1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium" title="Jaber Al-Ahmad International Stadium">Jaber Al-Ahmad International Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_City" title="Kuwait City">Kuwait City</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Kuwait. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Football_Association" title="Kuwait Football Association">Kuwait Football Association</a> (KFA) is the governing body of football in Kuwait. The KFA organises the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">men's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Kuwait women's national football team">women's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> national teams. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwaiti Premier League">Kuwaiti Premier League</a> is the top league of Kuwaiti football, featuring eighteen teams. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">Kuwait national football team</a> have been the champions of the <a href="/wiki/1980_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1980 AFC Asian Cup">1980 AFC Asian Cup</a>, runners-up of the <a href="/wiki/1976_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1976 AFC Asian Cup">1976 AFC Asian Cup</a>, and have taken third place of the <a href="/wiki/1984_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1984 AFC Asian Cup">1984 AFC Asian Cup</a>. Kuwait has also been to one FIFA World Cup, in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>; they drew 1–1 with <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a> before losing to <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, failing to advance from the first round. Kuwait is home to many football clubs including <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_(Kuwait)" title="Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)">Al-Arabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fahaheel_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fahaheel (football club)">Al-Fahaheel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jahra_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Jahra (football club)">Al-Jahra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Kuwait_Kaifan" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Kuwait Kaifan">Al-Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Naser_Sporting_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Naser Sporting Club">Al-Naser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Salmiya_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Salmiya Club">Al-Salmiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabab_(Kuwait)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Shabab (Kuwait)">Al-Shabab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qadsia Kuwait">Al Qadsia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Yarmouk_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Yarmouk (football club)">Al-Yarmouk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Kazma_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Kazma Kuwait">Kazma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaitan" title="Khaitan">Khaitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulaibikhat" title="Sulaibikhat">Sulaibikhat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahel_(Kuwaiti_football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahel (Kuwaiti football club)">Sahel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tadamon,_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Tadamon, Kuwait">Tadamon</a>. The biggest football rivalry in Kuwait is between <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_(Kuwait)" title="Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)">Al-Arabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qadsia Kuwait">Al Qadsia</a>. </p>
      <p>Basketball is one of the country's most popular sports. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait national basketball team">Kuwait national basketball team</a> is governed by the Kuwait Basketball Association (KBA). Kuwait made its international debut in 1959. The national team has been to the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Asian_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA Asian Championship">FIBA Asian Championship</a> in basketball eleven times. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Division_I_Basketball_League" title="Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League">Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League</a> is the highest professional basketball league in Kuwait. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_cricket_team" title="Kuwait national cricket team">Cricket in Kuwait</a> is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Cricket_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Cricket Association">Kuwait Cricket Association</a>. Other growing sports include <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Kuwait" title="Rugby union in Kuwait">rugby union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_men%27s_national_handball_team" title="Kuwait men's national handball team">Handball</a> is widely considered to be the national icon of Kuwait, although football is more popular among the overall population. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_ice_hockey_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait national ice hockey team">Ice hockey in Kuwait</a> is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Ice_Hockey_Association" title="Kuwait Ice Hockey Association">Kuwait Ice Hockey Association</a>. Kuwait first joined the <a href="/wiki/International_Ice_Hockey_Federation" title="International Ice Hockey Federation">International Ice Hockey Federation</a> in 1985, but was expelled in 1992 due to a lack of ice hockey activity.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup> Kuwait was re-admitted into the IIHF in May 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup> In 2015, Kuwait won the <a href="/wiki/IIHF_Challenge_Cup_of_Asia" title="IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia">IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2020 Kuwait held for the first time a leg of the <a href="/wiki/Aquabike_World_Championship_(powerboating)" title="Aquabike World Championship (powerboating)">UIM Aquabike World Championship</a> in front of Marina Beach City.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Kuwait.svg/32px-Flag_of_Kuwait.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Kuwait.svg/48px-Flag_of_Kuwait.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Kuwait.svg/64px-Flag_of_Kuwait.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Kuwait" title="Portal:Kuwait">Kuwait portal</a></span></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/scr/2013/cr13337.pdf">"Kuwait: Selected Issues"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. p.&nbsp;17. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141030072718/http://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/scr/2013/cr13337.pdf">Archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on 30 October 2014. <q>Kuwait has higher female labor market participation than other GCC countries; further improvements in labor force participation can support future growth prospects. Kuwait's labor force participation rate for Kuwaiti women (53 percent) is slightly above the world average (51 percent) and much higher than the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a> average (21 percent).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Kuwait%3A+Selected+Issues&amp;rft.pages=17&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imf.org%2Fexternal%2Fpubs%2Fft%2Fscr%2F2013%2Fcr13337.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AKuwait" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

        <li>
